href="/wiki/Cooking#History" title="Cooking">cooking</a></div></div></td></tr></tbody></table><table role="presentation" style="position:absolute;z-index:15;top:0.600em;left:0em;transform:translateY(-50%);padding:0;margin:0;font-size:100%"><tbody><tr><td style="padding:0;text-align:left;vertical-align:middle"><span style="color:black">←</span></td><td style="padding:0;text-align:left;vertical-align:middle"><div class="annot-nudge" style="font-size:100%;float:left;position:relative;top:0.5em"><div style="z-index:10;font-size:90%;color:black;display:block;line-height:105%;bottom:0"><a href="/wiki/Clothing#Early_use" title="Clothing">Earliest clothes</a></div></div></td></tr></tbody></table><table role="presentation" style="position:absolute;z-index:15;top:0.250em;left:0em;transform:translateY(-50%);padding:0;margin:0;font-size:100%"><tbody><tr><td style="padding:0;text-align:left;vertical-align:middle"><span style="color:black">←</span></td><td style="padding:0;text-align:left;vertical-align:middle"><div class="annot-nudge" style="font-size:100%;float:left;position:relative;top:0em"><div style="z-index:10;font-size:90%;color:black;display:block;line-height:105%;bottom:0"><a href="/wiki/Behavioral_modernity" title="Behavioral modernity">Modern humans</a></div></div></td></tr></tbody></table><div class="annot-bar" style="width:auto;font-size:100%;position:absolute;text-align:center;margin-top:21.000em"><div class="annot-nudge" style="font-size:100%;float:left;position:relative;text-align:left;top:-0.75em;left:-5em;width:8.8em"><div style="position:relative;width:auto;z-index:10;font-size:90%;color:black;vertical-align:middle;line-height:105%;bottom:0"><span style="display:block; text-align:center;"><b><a href="/wiki/Hominidae" title="Hominidae"><br/>H<br/><br/>o<br/><br/>m<br/><br/>i<br/><br/>n<br/><br/>i<br/><br/>d<br/><br/>s</a></b></span></div></div></div></td></tr><tr><td colspan="3" id="Caption" style="padding:0;margin:0 0.2em 0.7em 0.2em"><div class="toccolours" id="Caption" style="margin:0 0.5em;border-style:none;clear:both;text-align:center;width:26.8em"><div style="float:left;font-size:85%;">(<a href="/wiki/Myr" title="Myr">million years ago</a>)</div></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_evolution" title="Human evolution">Human evolution</a></div>
<p>A small African ape living around 6 Ma was the last animal whose descendants would include both modern humans and their closest relatives, the <a href="/wiki/Pan_(genus)" title="Pan (genus)">chimpanzees</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dawkins-Ancestors_124-8"><a href="#cite_note-Dawkins-Ancestors-124">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 100–101">: 100–101 </span></sup> Only two branches of its family tree have surviving descendants. Very soon after the split, for reasons that are still unclear, apes in one branch developed the ability to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bipedal" title="Bipedal">walk upright</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dawkins-Ancestors_124-9"><a href="#cite_note-Dawkins-Ancestors-124">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 95–99">: 95–99 </span></sup> <a href="/wiki/Brain" title="Brain">Brain</a> size increased rapidly, and by 2 Ma, the first animals classified in the genus <i><a href="/wiki/Homo" title="Homo">Homo</a></i> had appeared.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fortey_167-1"><a href="#cite_note-Fortey-167">[166]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 300">: 300 </span></sup> Of course, the line between different species or even genera is somewhat arbitrary as organisms continuously change over generations. Around the same time, the other branch split into the ancestors of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Common_chimpanzee" title="Common chimpanzee">common chimpanzee</a> and the ancestors of the <a href="/wiki/Bonobo" title="Bonobo">bonobo</a> as evolution continued simultaneously in all life forms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dawkins-Ancestors_124-10"><a href="#cite_note-Dawkins-Ancestors-124">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 100–101">: 100–101 </span></sup>
</p><p>The ability to control <a href="/wiki/Fire" title="Fire">fire</a> probably began in <i><a href="/wiki/Homo_erectus" title="Homo erectus">Homo erectus</a></i> (or <i><a href="/wiki/Homo_ergaster" title="Homo ergaster">Homo ergaster</a></i>), probably at least 790,000 years ago<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-goren-inbar_192-0"><a href="#cite_note-goren-inbar-192">[191]</a></sup> but perhaps as early as 1.5 Ma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dawkins-Ancestors_124-11"><a href="#cite_note-Dawkins-Ancestors-124">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 67">: 67 </span></sup> The use and discovery of controlled fire may even predate <i>Homo erectus</i>. Fire was possibly used by the early <a href="/wiki/Lower_Paleolithic" title="Lower Paleolithic">Lower Paleolithic</a> (<a href="/wiki/Oldowan" title="Oldowan">Oldowan</a>) hominid <i><a href="/wiki/Homo_habilis" title="Homo habilis">Homo habilis</a></i> or strong <a href="/wiki/Australopithecine" title="Australopithecine">australopithecines</a> such as <i><a href="/wiki/Paranthropus" title="Paranthropus">Paranthropus</a>.</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McClellan_193-0"><a href="#cite_note-McClellan-193">[192]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Human_evolution_chart-en.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="544" decoding="async" height="243" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Human_evolution_chart-en.svg/220px-Human_evolution_chart-en.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Human_evolution_chart-en.svg/330px-Human_evolution_chart-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Human_evolution_chart-en.svg/440px-Human_evolution_chart-en.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Human_evolution_chart-en.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A reconstruction of human history based on fossil data.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[193]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>It is more difficult to establish the <a href="/wiki/Origin_of_language" title="Origin of language">origin of language</a>; it is unclear whether <i>Homo erectus</i> could speak or if that capability had not begun until <i>Homo sapiens</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dawkins-Ancestors_124-12"><a href="#cite_note-Dawkins-Ancestors-124">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 67">: 67 </span></sup> As brain size increased, babies were born earlier, before their heads grew too large to pass through the <a href="/wiki/Pelvis" title="Pelvis">pelvis</a>. As a result, they exhibited more <a href="/wiki/Neuroplasticity" title="Neuroplasticity">plasticity</a>, and thus possessed an increased capacity to learn and required a longer period of dependence. Social skills became more complex, language became more sophisticated, and tools became more elaborate. This contributed to further cooperation and intellectual development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McNeill_195-0"><a href="#cite_note-McNeill-195">[194]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 7">: 7 </span></sup> Modern humans (<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Homo_sapiens" title="Homo sapiens">Homo sapiens</a></i>) are believed to have originated around 200,000 years ago or earlier <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Single-origin_hypothesis" title="Single-origin hypothesis">in Africa</a>; the oldest fossils date back to around 160,000 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gibbons_196-0"><a href="#cite_note-gibbons-196">[195]</a></sup>
</p><p>The first humans to show signs of <a href="/wiki/Spirituality" title="Spirituality">spirituality</a> are the <a href="/wiki/Neanderthal" title="Neanderthal">Neanderthals</a> (usually classified as a separate species with no surviving descendants); they buried their dead, often with no sign of food or tools.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hopfe_197-0"><a href="#cite_note-hopfe-197">[196]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 17">: 17 </span></sup> However, evidence of more sophisticated beliefs, such as the early <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cro-Magnon" title="Cro-Magnon">Cro-Magnon</a> <a href="/wiki/Cave_painting" title="Cave painting">cave paintings</a> (probably with magical or religious significance)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hopfe_197-1"><a href="#cite_note-hopfe-197">[196]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 17–19">: 17–19 </span></sup> did not appear until 32,000 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chauvet_198-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chauvet-198">[197]</a></sup> Cro-Magnons also left behind stone figurines such as <a href="/wiki/Venus_of_Willendorf" title="Venus of Willendorf">Venus of Willendorf</a>, probably also signifying religious belief.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hopfe_197-2"><a href="#cite_note-hopfe-197">[196]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 17–19">: 17–19 </span></sup> By 11,000 years ago, <i>Homo sapiens</i> had reached the southern tip of <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>, the last of the uninhabited continents (except for Antarctica, which remained undiscovered until 1820 AD).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oxford-atlas_199-0"><a href="#cite_note-oxford-atlas-199">[198]</a></sup> Tool use and communication continued to improve, and interpersonal relationships became more intricate.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_history">Human history</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Human_history" title="Human history">Human history</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cradle_of_civilization" title="Cradle of civilization">Cradle of civilization</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Africa" title="History of Africa">History of Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Americas" title="History of the Americas">History of the Americas</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Antarctica" title="History of Antarctica">History of Antarctica</a>, and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Eurasia" title="History of Eurasia">History of Eurasia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Da_Vinci_Vitruve_Luc_Viatour_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2966" data-file-width="2155" decoding="async" height="303" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Da_Vinci_Vitruve_Luc_Viatour_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Da_Vinci_Vitruve_Luc_Viatour_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Da_Vinci_Vitruve_Luc_Viatour_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Da_Vinci_Vitruve_Luc_Viatour_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Da_Vinci_Vitruve_Luc_Viatour_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Da_Vinci_Vitruve_Luc_Viatour_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Da_Vinci_Vitruve_Luc_Viatour_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Vitruvian_Man" title="Vitruvian Man">Vitruvian Man</a> by <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_da_Vinci" title="Leonardo da Vinci">Leonardo da Vinci</a> epitomizes the advances in art and science seen during the Renaissance.</div></div></div>
<p>Throughout more than 90% of its history, <i>Homo sapiens</i> lived in small bands as <a href="/wiki/Nomad" title="Nomad">nomadic</a> <a href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherer" title="Hunter-gatherer">hunter-gatherers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McNeill_195-1"><a href="#cite_note-McNeill-195">[194]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 8">: 8 </span></sup> As language became more complex, the ability to remember and communicate information resulted, according to a theory proposed by <a href="/wiki/Richard_Dawkins" title="Richard Dawkins">Richard Dawkins</a>, in a new replicator: the <a href="/wiki/Meme" title="Meme">meme</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dawkins-sg_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-dawkins-sg-200">[199]</a></sup> Ideas could be exchanged quickly and passed down the generations. <a href="/wiki/Cultural_evolution" title="Cultural evolution">Cultural evolution</a> quickly outpaced <a href="/wiki/Evolution" title="Evolution">biological evolution</a>, and <a href="/wiki/History" title="History">history</a> proper began. Between 8500 and 7000 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Before_Christ" title="Before Christ">BC</a>, humans in the <a href="/wiki/Fertile_Crescent" title="Fertile Crescent">Fertile Crescent</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a> began the systematic husbandry of plants and animals: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tudge_201-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tudge-201">[200]</a></sup> This spread to neighboring regions, and developed independently elsewhere, until most <i>Homo sapiens</i> lived sedentary lives in permanent settlements as farmers. Not all societies abandoned nomadism, especially those in isolated areas of the globe poor in <a href="/wiki/Domestication" title="Domestication">domesticable</a> plant species, such as <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-diamond_202-0"><a href="#cite_note-diamond-202">[201]</a></sup> However, among those civilizations that did adopt agriculture, the relative stability and increased productivity provided by farming allowed the population to expand.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Agriculture had a major impact; humans began to affect the environment as never before. Surplus food allowed a priestly or governing class to arise, followed by increasing <a href="/wiki/Division_of_labour" title="Division of labour">division of labor</a>. This led to Earth's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_civilization" title="First civilization">first civilization</a> at <a href="/wiki/Sumer" title="Sumer">Sumer</a> in the Middle East, between 4000 and 3000 BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McNeill_195-2"><a href="#cite_note-McNeill-195">[194]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 15">: 15 </span></sup> Additional civilizations quickly arose in <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egypt" title="Ancient Egypt">ancient Egypt</a>, at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indus_Valley_civilisation" title="Indus Valley civilisation">Indus River valley</a> and in China. The invention of <a href="/wiki/Writing" title="Writing">writing</a> enabled complex societies to arise: record-keeping and <a href="/wiki/Library" title="Library">libraries</a> served as a storehouse of knowledge and increased the cultural transmission of information. Humans no longer had to spend all their time working for survival, enabling the first specialized occupations (e.g. craftsmen, merchants, priests, etc.). Curiosity and education drove the pursuit of knowledge and wisdom, and various disciplines, including <a href="/wiki/Science" title="Science">science</a> (in a primitive form), arose. This in turn led to the emergence of increasingly larger and more complex civilizations, such as the first empires, which at times traded with one another, or fought for territory and resources.
</p><p>By around 500 BC, there were advanced civilizations in the Middle East, Iran, India, China, and Greece, at times expanding, at times entering into decline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McNeill_195-3"><a href="#cite_note-McNeill-195">[194]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 3">: 3 </span></sup> In 221 BC, China became a single polity that would grow to spread its culture throughout <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">East Asia</a>, and it has remained the most populous nation in the world. During this period, famous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">Hindu</a> texts known as <a href="/wiki/Vedas" title="Vedas">vedas</a> came in existence in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indus_valley_civilization" title="Indus valley civilization">Indus valley civilization</a>. This civilization developed in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Warfare" title="Warfare">warfare</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arts" title="Arts">arts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Science" title="Science">science</a>, mathematics and in <a href="/wiki/Architect" title="Architect">architect</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The fundamentals of <a class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Western_civilization" title="Western civilization">Western civilization</a> were largely shaped in <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Ancient Greece</a>, with the world's first <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democratic government</a> and major advances in philosophy and <a href="/wiki/Science" title="Science">science</a>, and in <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Ancient Rome</a> with advances in law, government, and engineering.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Daly2013_203-0"><a href="#cite_note-Daly2013-203">[202]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> was <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_ancient_Rome#History_of_Roman_religion" title="Religion in ancient Rome">Christianized by Emperor Constantine</a> in the early 4th century and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Decline_of_the_Roman_Empire" title="Decline of the Roman Empire">declined</a> by the end of the 5th. Beginning with the 7th century, <a href="/wiki/Christianization#Christianization_of_Europe_(5th–9th_centuries)" title="Christianization">Christianization of Europe</a> began, and since at least the 4th century <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> has played a <a href="/wiki/Role_of_Christianity_in_civilization" title="Role of Christianity in civilization">prominent role</a> in the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Western_civilization" title="History of Western civilization">shaping of Western civilization</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[203]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Caltron_J.H_Hayas_205-0"><a href="#cite_note-Caltron_J.H_Hayas-205">[204]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Orlandis_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-Orlandis-206">[205]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-How_The_Catholic_Church_Built_Western_Civilization_207-0"><a href="#cite_note-How_The_Catholic_Church_Built_Western_Civilization-207">[206]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Perry2012_208-0"><a href="#cite_note-Perry2012-208">[207]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[208]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[209]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[210]</a></sup> In 610, <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> was founded and quickly became the dominant religion in <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Western Asia</a>. The <a href="/wiki/House_of_Wisdom" title="House of Wisdom">House of Wisdom</a> was established in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abbasid" title="Abbasid">Abbasid</a>-era <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[211]</a></sup> It is considered to have been a major intellectual center during the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age" title="Islamic Golden Age">Islamic Golden Age</a>, where Muslim scholars in <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a> flourished from the ninth to the thirteenth centuries until the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongol_sack_of_Baghdad" title="Mongol sack of Baghdad">Mongol sack of Baghdad</a> in 1258 AD. In 1054 AD the <a href="/wiki/East%E2%80%93West_Schism" title="East–West Schism">Great Schism</a> between the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Church</a> led to the prominent cultural differences between <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BideleuxJeffries48_213-0"><a href="#cite_note-BideleuxJeffries48-213">[212]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 14th century, the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a> began in <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> with advances in religion, art, and science.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McNeill_195-4"><a href="#cite_note-McNeill-195">[194]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 317–319">: 317–319 </span></sup> At that time the Christian Church as a political entity lost much of its power. In 1492, <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> reached the Americas, initiating great changes to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_world" title="New world">new world</a>. European civilization began to change beginning in 1500, leading to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scientific_revolution" title="Scientific revolution">scientific</a> and <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">industrial</a> revolutions.  That continent began to exert political and cultural <a href="/wiki/Hegemony" title="Hegemony">dominance</a> over human societies around the world, a time known as the <a href="/wiki/History_of_colonialism" title="History of colonialism">Colonial era</a> (also see <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">Age of Discovery</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McNeill_195-5"><a href="#cite_note-McNeill-195">[194]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 295–299">: 295–299 </span></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_events">Recent events</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bruce_McCandless_II_during_EVA_in_1984.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3072" data-file-width="3072" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Bruce_McCandless_II_during_EVA_in_1984.jpg/220px-Bruce_McCandless_II_during_EVA_in_1984.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Bruce_McCandless_II_during_EVA_in_1984.jpg/330px-Bruce_McCandless_II_during_EVA_in_1984.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Bruce_McCandless_II_during_EVA_in_1984.jpg/440px-Bruce_McCandless_II_during_EVA_in_1984.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bruce_McCandless_II_during_EVA_in_1984.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Astronaut <a href="/wiki/Bruce_McCandless_II" title="Bruce McCandless II">Bruce McCandless II</a> outside of the <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">Space Shuttle</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Challenger" title="Space Shuttle Challenger">Challenger</a></i> in 1984</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Late_modern_period" title="Late modern period">Late modern period</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Modernity" title="Modernity">Modernity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Future" title="Future">Future</a></div>
<p>Change has continued at a rapid pace from the mid-1940s to today. Technological developments include <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapon" title="Nuclear weapon">nuclear weapons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Computer" title="Computer">computers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Genetic_engineering" title="Genetic engineering">genetic engineering</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nanotechnology" title="Nanotechnology">nanotechnology</a>. <a href="/wiki/Economic_globalization" title="Economic globalization">Economic globalization</a>, spurred by advances in communication and transportation technology, has influenced everyday life in many parts of the world. Cultural and institutional forms such as <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">capitalism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Environmentalism" title="Environmentalism">environmentalism</a> have increased influence. Major concerns and problems such as <a href="/wiki/Disease" title="Disease">disease</a>, <a href="/wiki/War" title="War">war</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poverty" title="Poverty">poverty</a>, violent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Political_radicalism" title="Political radicalism">radicalism</a>, and recently, human-caused <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">climate change</a> have risen as the world population increases.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>In 1957, the Soviet Union launched <a href="/wiki/Sputnik_1" title="Sputnik 1">the first artificial satellite</a> into orbit and, soon afterward, <a href="/wiki/Yuri_Gagarin" title="Yuri Gagarin">Yuri Gagarin</a> became the first human in space.  <a href="/wiki/Neil_Armstrong" title="Neil Armstrong">Neil Armstrong</a>, an American, was the first to set foot on another astronomical object, the Moon. Unmanned probes have been sent to all the known planets in the Solar System, with some (such as the two <a href="/wiki/Voyager_program" title="Voyager program">Voyager</a> spacecraft) having left the Solar System. Five space agencies, representing over fifteen countries,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Human_214-0"><a href="#cite_note-Human-214">[213]</a></sup>  have worked together to build the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a>. Aboard it, there has been a continuous human presence in space since 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Expedit_215-0"><a href="#cite_note-Expedit-215">[214]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Web" title="World Wide Web">World Wide Web</a> became a part of everyday life in the 1990s, and since then has become an indispensable source of information in the <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">developed world</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
